Write a negative review about a bad book:  This book was poorly written and poorly edited. The book claims to be an "unbiased look at the history of women's rights," but the truth is that it is full of inaccuracies and outright lies. The author claims that women's suffrage is the "greatest triumph of the feminist movement." Write a negative review about a bad book:  The book is filled with errors, including the claim that a "majority" of the Jews of Poland converted to Christianity. In reality, only a small minority of the Polish Jews converted to Catholicism. This is one of the main reasons why many Jews do not like the book. The book claims that only a few Jewish doctors were in Poland during the Inquisition, but there is no proof that such a large number ever existed. The claim that the Jews were forced into the ghettos by the Catholic Church is also false, since many of the Jewish converts to Catholicism were wealthy. This book also states that the Germans were forced to give the Jews their land back after the war, but this is a blatant lie as well. There were no land exchanges and the Germans even made sure that the property rights of the German Jews were honored. The entire book is a lie. I gave it three poor reviews instead of one because I just gave up on trying to read the book: 1. The assertion that "the majority of the Poles converted to Christian faith" is also untrue. According to the Encyclopedia of Religion and Ethics, only about 7 percent of the population converted to Protestantism and only about 6 percent to Catholicism, with the rest remaining Catholic. 2. The contention that "The Holocaust was not a tragedy for the Jews, but a success for the Christian Church" is equally inaccurate. According the Encyclopedia, "For the majority of survivors, the war was the single greatest disaster of their lives." The majority of Jews who were killed by the Nazis were killed because they refused to convert to Christianity and/or refused to work in the Nazi economy. They were executed on the spot or sent to the death camps, which were designed specifically to kill all non-Christians. 3. The notion that the Nazis "converted to Christianity" and then "reverted to Judaism" is pure nonsense. It is the belief of the book that Jews who converted to Islam and Christianity were forced out of their homes and sent to concentration camps. This also has no basis in fact. 4. The claims that "most Jews never accepted Christianity" are also baseless. According Dr. Martin Kramer, a leading authority on Jewish history, it was the Catholic priests, not the Protestant or Orthodox rabbis, who converted the Jews. In fact, according to Kramer, the Jews converted first, then the Orthodox rabbinical leaders followed. 5. The fact that the book contains errors makes it worthless.

Write a negative review about a bad book:  The book is filled with bad advice about marriage. It's based on bad research, but I'm afraid the bad news doesn't end there. I bought the book expecting a good review about good book, but instead I received bad advice. The advice includes "Be careful what you wish for" and "It's better to be the person you want than the one you get." This is bad advice for a number of reasons: 1. The research the authors cite is extremely dubious. The authors state that studies show that women who have more than three abortions have a higher chance of getting cancer, but when the studies were replicated, the results showed the opposite. The reason the original research is flawed is because the women were given fake names and the women who were most likely to get cancer had the least amount of abortions. The researchers did not account for this problem. The study does not say anything about the effect of having three or more children on a woman's chances of getting pregnant again. The book states that one study shows that women with multiple abortions have "higher risk of becoming addicted to drugs and alcohol," but the study does nothing to explain the lack of control for confounding variables. 2. The conclusion the book draws about women's happiness is false. The conclusions that the book gives about women "missing their happy marriages" is not supported by the data. The author's statement that "the best marriages are the ones that don't last" is also false. A good marriage is one that is happy, successful, and happy to be married. It isn't the happiest marriages that fail, it's the ones who never make it to the end. The failure rate for the book is unacceptable, and the authors should be ashamed of themselves. 3. The bad advice is based on the flawed research that is given in the book. If the research had been done properly, the authors would have discovered that the best marriages were the ones without children. They would have learned that children don't bring happiness.  4. The "Be Careful What You Wish For" and the "It Is Better to Be the Person You Want Than the One You Get" quotes are false. Women who have multiple abortions are less likely to be happy in their marriages. They are less successful in getting pregnant. If you want to have a good marriage, have only one child.

Write a negative review about a bad book:  The book contains numerous errors, including the statement that "the British Empire was a colonial power". The British Empire, which is the largest and most powerful empire in the world, never colonized any country, let alone Africa. The empire that the author refers to, the American Empire, was a British creation, and the United States has never colonated any country.  I have spent countless hours and dollars on books and research and this book leaves me with the feeling that I wasted my money and time. I'm so angry with the book that I'm going to give it a bad review: I could not put it down. The book is so poorly written and poorly edited that it's laughable.  It's not just the spelling and grammar errors, it's the poor information. The authors state that the "British were the original colonists to America, but the word 'colony' was first used in America by the Dutch." It's so obvious that this is a blatant lie.  There's nothing about the Dutch that resembles the British, or any European, culture whatsoever. The American Colonies were founded by the French, and were known as the "French America" colonies. The French were the ones who first settled in North America, and they called the new land "New France". The word "colony" never appeared in any official document or in any written work by the British government or any official of the American government. In fact, the French never called the land "America" at all. Instead, they referred to the land as "La Nouvelle France".  The author's "history" about the English being the original settlers and settlers in the American colonies is a complete fabrication. The English didn't come to America until 1607, after the French had already settled the land. It was only in 1765 that the British actually declared themselves the "owners" of the land in the Declaration of Independence.  The "British" colonies never "colonized" any land in Africa. There is absolutely no evidence that the English ever even attempted to do so. They were never invited to, nor were they allowed to, even attempt to establish a colony. It's a complete fraud to suggest that the colonies ever "coloned" Africa.
